Jamison Brereton

185
Heaven and Earth
Agastya Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This eleven-verse hymn falls into two connected sections. Verses 2тАУ8 all end with a p─Бda-long refrain; since this refrain seems to be an implicit response to verse 1, we believe that 1тАУ8 form a coherent whole, ending with an expiatory verse (8) and then followed by a three-verse summary referring to the hymn-within-a-hymn that precedes.
The refrain addressed to Heaven and Earth, тАЬprotect us from the formless void,тАЭ expresses the Vedic fear of the darkness and lack of definition character istic of pre-creation chaos. Heaven and Earth help dispel that fear and provide protection from the void in several ways. They are the defining structures of the cosmos, and within the shaped space they produce between them, all separate forms, animate and inanimate, exist. This seems to be the point of verse 1c, тАЬthey carry everything that is a nameтАЭ; we take this as a version of the later Sanskrit n─Бma-r┼лpa тАЬname and form,тАЭ the multiplicity of individual entities, defined by the conjunction of a physical form and a word for it. Heaven and Earth are also the parents of the Sun, the light that allows the individual forms to be seen. Their parentage of the Sun is, in our opinion, the subject of verses 2тАУ4, though the Sun is not mentioned directly. The embryo of verse 2 is the тАЬgift of AditiтАЭ in verse 3 (the Sun is already called ─Бdity├б, son of Aditi in the late R╠еgveda; see, e.g., I.191.9), while verse 4 describes the wonder that Heaven and Earth are never burned by the Sun, their son. (On this kinship relation, see also the Heaven and Earth hymn I.160.)
Heaven and Earth define space, but they also, in part via their son, define time: the regular alternation of day and night is first mentioned in verse 1d. The two complementary pairs, Heaven and Earth and Night and Dawn, are treated together in verse 4c, and in our opinion the siblings of verse 5 are more likely Night and Dawn than Heaven and Earth, since they are located тАЬin the lap of their parents,тАЭ that is, Heaven and Earth. However, the latter pair are definitely the subject of verses 6тАУ7, and their role in conception is highlighted again. The final verse of the refrain-bounded section (8) seeks expiation for an unnamed offense, and offers the current hymn (тАЬthis hymnic visionтАЭ) to that end.
The last three verses (9тАУ11) develop this theme. The poet expresses the hope that the verbal products he has just produced will help him: his тАЬlauds belonging to menтАЭ (a variation on the technical term n├бr─Б┼Ы├бс╣Гsa, vs. 9), and the тАЬtruthтАЭ he addressed to Heaven and Earth (vss. 10тАУ11).

рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ рдирд┐рд░реБрдХреНрддрдВ рджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhich of these two, (Heaven and Earth), is prior which posterior; how were they engendered; (declare), sages, who knows this? verily, you uphold the universe of itself, and the days (and nights) revolve as if they had wheels.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Days and nights revolve: ahan cakriyeva, two days as if wheeled; i.e. the succession of day and night, each of which may be considered in turn as preceding or folliowing the other, like the rotations of a wheel

Jamison Brereton

Which of these two is the earlier, and which the later? How were they born, o poets? Who fully understands?
By themselves the two carry everything that is a name. Day and Night roll through (them) like two wheels.

Griffith

WHETHER of these is elder, whether later? How were they born? Who knoweth it, ye sages?
These of themselves support all things existing: as on a car the Day and Night roll onward.

Macdonell

Which of the two is earlier, which the later? How were they born, ye sages, who discerns it? They by themselves support all things existing. As with a wheel the day and night roll onward.

Geldner

Welche von diesen beiden ist die fr├╝here, welche die sp├дtere? Wie sind sie entstanden, ihr Seher? Wer wei├Я es genau? Alles tragen sie selbst, was ein Name ist. Es drehen sich die beiden Tagesh├дlften wie R├дder um.

Grassmann

Wer ist von beiden fr├╝her? wer die sp├дtre? und wie erzeugt? ihr Weisen, wer entscheidet? Sie beide wahrlich tragen alle Wesen, der Tag, die Nacht, auf einem Rad sich drehend.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдЪрд░рдиреНрддреА рдЕрд╡рд┐рдЪрд▓реЗ рджреНрд╡реЗ рдПрд╡ рдПрддреЗ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреМ рднреВрд░рд┐ рдмрд╣реБрддрд░рдВ рдЪрд░рдиреНрддрдВ рдкрджреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдВ рдкрд╛рджрдпреБрдХреНрддрдВ рдЧрд░реНрднрд╡рджрд╛рд╢реНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рдХреГрддреНрд╕реНрдирдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдЬрд╛рддрдореН рдЕрдкрджреА рд╕реНрд╡рдпрдВ рдкрд╛рджрд░рд╣рд┐рддреЗ рджрдзрд╛рддреЗ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрддрдГ ред рдЕрдирдпреЛрд░реНрдордзреНрдпреЗ рдЦрд▓реБ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рдЬрдЧрддреН рдХреНрд╖реЗрдореЗрдг рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ ред рдзрд╛рд░рдгреЗ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдГ ред рдкрд┐рддреНрд░реЛрдГ рдорд╛рддрд╛рдкрд┐рддреНрд░реЛрдГ рдЙрдкрд╕реНрдереЗ рдЙрддреНрд╕рдЩреНрдЧреЗ рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдирдВ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрдВ рдзреНрд░реБрд╡рдорд╛рддреНрдордЬрдВ рд╕реВрдиреБрдВ рди рдкреБрддреНрд░рдорд┐рд╡ рдпрдерд╛ рд╕реНрдиреЗрд╣реЗрди рд╡рд░реНрдзрдпрдиреНрддреМ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрддреМ рдорд╛рддрд╛рдкрд┐рддрд░реМ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН ред рдЕрде рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖реЗрдгрд╛рд╣ред рд╣реЗ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреМ ред рдЗрддрд░реЗрддрд░рд╛рдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рдпрд╛ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреНрд╡рдореБрднрдпреЛрдГ ред рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдЕрднреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдорд╣рддреЛ рднрдпрд╣реЗрддреЛрдГ рдкрд╛рдкрд╛рддреН рд░рдХреНрд╖рддрдВ рдкрд╛рд▓рдпрддрдореН ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдЕрднреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдЕрднреНрд╡рдВ рдорд╣рддреН ред рдЕрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдЕрднреНрд╡реЗрддрд┐ рдорд╣рдиреНрдирд╛рдо рее рджреНрд╡рдиреНрджреНрд╡реЗ рдХреГрддрджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рджреЗрд╢рд╕реНрдп рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрд╢рдмреНрджрд╕реНрдп рдордзреНрдпреЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рддрдореН рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрджрдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧрд╢реНрдЫрдиреНрджрд╕рдГред рдЖрдордиреНрддреНрд░рд┐рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирддреНрд╡реЗрди рдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрд╛рднрд╛рд╡рдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFootless and motionless, they sustain numerous moving and footed races, as a son is even (nursed) on the lap of his parents; defend us, Heaven and Earth, from great (danger).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Rakс╣гatam no abhv─Бt = great; the substantive is supplied: from sin as the cause of great danger: mahato bhayahetaс╕е p─Бp─Бt

Jamison Brereton

The two, unmoving and footless, conceive an ample embryo, moving and footed,
like a natural son in the lap of his parents. тАУ O Heaven and Earth,
protect us from the formless void.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, I consider the embryo here to be the sun, but various other identifications have been proposed.

Griffith

The Twain uphold, though motionless and footless, a widespread offspring having feet and moving.
Like your own son upon his parents’ bosom, protect us, Heaven and earth, from fearful danger.

Macdonell

The two support, though moving not and footless, Abundant offspring having feet and moving. O Heaven and Earth, from dreadful darkness save us, Like your own son held in his parents’ bosom.

Geldner

Die beiden, ohne selbst zu gehen, fu├Яlos, empfangen die gehende, fu├Яbegabte, zahlreiche Leibesfrucht wie einen leiblichen Sohn im Scho├Яe, der Eltern. - Himmel und Erde, bewahret uns vor ├Ьbergewalt!

Grassmann

Sie beide, fusslos und nicht wandernd, tragen als Frucht das Volk, was F├╝sse hat und wandert; Gleichwie den eignen Sohn im Schooss der Aeltern beschirmt vor grauser Noth uns, Erd’ und Himmel!

Elizarenkova

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рднреВрд░рд┐рдореН) рдмрд╣реБрдореН (рджреНрд╡реЗ) (рдЕрдЪрд░рдиреНрддреА) рдЗрддрд╕реНрддрддрдГ рд╕реНрд╡рдХрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рдп рдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╣рд┐рддреЗ (рдЪрд░рдиреНрддрдореН) рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрдореН (рдкрджреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдореН) рдмрд╣рд╡рдГ рдкрд╛рджрд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдБрд╕реНрддрдореН (рдЧрд░реНрднрдореН) рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрдореН (рдЕрдкрджреА) рдЕрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдкрд╛рджреЗ (рджрдзрд╛рддреЗ) (рдирд┐рддреНрдпрдореН) (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рд╕реВрдиреБрдореН) (рдкрд┐рддреНрд░реЛрдГ) (рдЙрдкрд╕реНрдереЗ) (рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛) рджреНрдпреМрдГ (рд░рдХреНрд╖рддрдореН) (рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА) рднреВрдорд┐рдГ (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рдЕрднреНрд╡рд╛рддреН) рдЕрд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдЪрд░рдгрдЬрдиреНрдпрд╛рджреНрджреБрдГрдЦрд╛рддреН рее реи рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдЕрджрд┐рддреЗрдГ ред рдПрддрджрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдпреБрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдореН ред рдЕрдЦрдгреНрдбрдиреАрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдГ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╕реНрдп рдЪ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐ рджрд╛рддреНрд░рдВ рдзрдирдВ рд╣реБрд╡реЗ рдЖрд╣реНрд╡рдпрд╛рдорд┐ рд╕реНрдкреГрд╣рдпрд╛рдореАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдВ рддрджреНрдзрдирдореН ред рдЕрдиреЗрд╣рдГ рдЕрдкрд╛рдкрдВ рджреБрдГрдЦрд░рд╣рд┐рддрдВ рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рддреНрдордХрдореН рдЕрдирд░реНрд╡рдореН рдЕрдирд░рдгрдореН рдЕрдХреНрд╖реАрдгрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрд╡рддреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдГ рдлрд▓рднреВрддреЗрди рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдЧреЗрдг рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рдЕрд╡рдзрдореН рдЕрд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд┐рддрдВ рдирдорд╕реНрд╡рддреН рдЕрдиреНрдирд╡рддреН ред рдИрджреГрд╢рдВ рдзрдирдВ рд╣реБрд╡реЗ ред рддрддреН рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдХрд╛рдЩреНрдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрдореБрдХреНрддрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рдзрдирдВ рд╣реЗ рд░реЛрджрд╕реА рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреМ рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░реЗ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдп рдЬрдирдпрддрдореН рдЙрддреНрдкрд╛рджрдпрддрдореН ред рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡реЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рддрдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI solicit of Aditi, wealth, without pain or decay, like heaven (in fullness of enjoyment), exempt from injury, and abounding in food; grant, Heaven and Earth, such wealth to him who praises you; defend us, Heaven and Earth, from great (danger).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Aditi = the firmament

Jamison Brereton

I invoke the gift of Aditi, which is without fault, without aggression, without weapon, and provided with sunlight and reverence.
O you two world-halves, beget it for the singer. тАУ O Heaven and Earth, protect us from the formless void.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The them. adj. anarv├б- is clearly derived from the well-attested bahuvr─лhi - n-stem anarv├бn- (cf. also the thematized anarv├бс╣Зa-). The neut. NA to the n-stem should be *anarv├б, which is not found. In two instances in which it should modify a neut. acc. (I.37.1, VI.48.15) we find instead the masc. anarv─Б╠Бс╣Зam, an adjustment probably meant to make the form more transparent (see comm. on those two passages). As for the supposed them. stem anarv├б-, in two of the occurrences listed by Grassmann the referents are neut. (cakr├бm I.164.2, d─Бtr├бm here). In both passages the neut. NA anarv├бm comes at the end of an odd p─Бda before an even p─Бda beginning with a consonant. I think it is at least arguable that the original reading in both cases was *anarv├б, the expected neut. to the n-stem, which was redactionally altered to a thematic acc. The alternation has no metrical consequences. As for the other two forms that Grassmann lists to the them. stem, both (II.40.6, VII.40.4) qualify Aditi in the nom. sg. and have the form anarv─Б╠Б. I suggest that both actually belong to the n-stem, whose nom. sg. has exactly that form, and that they are fem., but do not exhibit the fem. derivational suffix -─л (expect *anarv├бс╣З─л-?).

Griffith

I call for Aditi’s unrivalled bounty, perfect, celestial, deathless, meet for worship.
Produce this, ye Twain Worlds, for him who lauds you. Protect us, Heaven and Earth, from fearful danger.

Macdonell

I crave of Aditi the gift, the matchless. Beneficent, illustrious, and honoured: O ye two worlds, procure that for the singer. O Heaven and Earth, from dreadful darkness save us.

Geldner

Die Gabe der Aditi errufe ich, die fehlerlose, unbestrittene, sonnenhafte, vom Tode befreiende, ehrfurchtgebietende. Diese schaffet dem S├дnger, ihr beide Rodasi. - Himmel und Erde, bewahret uns vor ├Ьbergewalt!

Grassmann

Der Aditi erhabne sichre Gabe, die heilsam, gl├дnzend, heilig ist erfleh’ ich, Das schafft dem S├дnger, o ihr Welten beide, beschirmt vor grauser Noth uns, Erd’ und Himmel!

Elizarenkova

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рдЕрд╡рд╕рд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рддреЛрд╜рдзрд┐рдХреЗрди рдХреЗрдирдЪрд┐рддреН рдХреГрддреЗрди рдЕрд╡рдиреЗрди рд╕рдореГрджреНрдзреНрдпрд╛ рдЕрддрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдиреЗ рдЕрдиреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░реЗ рее рддрдкреЗрдГ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдХрд░реНрдордгрдГ рдЗрджрдВ рд░реВрдкрдореН рее рдЕрддрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдиреЗ рдЕрдиреНрдпреИрд░рдкреАрдбреНрдпрдорд╛рдиреЗред ‘рдЕрд╡рд╕рд╛ рдЕрдиреЗрди рдЕрд╡рдиреНрддреА рддрд░реНрдкрдпрдиреНрддреНрдпреМ рджреЗрд╡рдкреБрддреНрд░реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд░реНрддрд╛рд░реЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреАрдпрд╛рдГ рдпрдпреЛрд╕реНрддрд╛рджреГрд╢реНрдпреМ ред рд▓реЛрдХрджреНрд╡рдпрд╕реНрдерд╛рдГ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рддрджреБрдкрдЬреАрд╡реНрдпрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛рдГ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдЪреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рдИрджреГрд╢реМ рдЙрднреЗ рд░реЛрджрд╕реА рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреМ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдореН рдЕрд╣реНрдирд╛рдореН ред рдПрддрджреНрд░рд╛рддреНрд░реЗрд░рдкреНрдпреБрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдореН ред рджреНрдпреЛрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдирд╛рдореН рдЕрд╣реНрдирд╛рдВ рд░рд╛рддреНрд░реАрдгрд╛рдВ рдЪ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдЙрднрдпрд╡рд┐рдзреИрдГ рд╢реАрддреЛрд╖реНрдгрд╛рджрд┐рд░реВрдкреИрдГ рд╡рд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгреИрдГ рдзрдиреИрдГ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрднреВрддреИрдГ ред рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд▓рд╛рднрд╛рдпреЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рддрджрд░реНрдердВ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдореН рдЕрдиреБ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо рдЕрдиреБрднрд╡реЗрдо ред рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреЛ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рддрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay we ever be (devoted to) that Heaven and Earth, who are not subject to annoyance, who satisfy (all beings) with food, who have the gods (and men) for sons, and who are both endowed with the double (condition) of the divine days (and nights); defend us, Heaven and Earth, from great (danger).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Divine days and nights: ubhe dev─Бn─Бm ubhayebhir ahn─Бm: ahan = night as well as day

Jamison Brereton

We should be devoted to the two who are never scorched, (always) giving help with their help, to the two world-halves whose children are the gods, to the pair among the gods, along with the pairs among the days. тАУ O Heaven and Earth, protect us from the formless void.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The lexeme ├бnu тИЪas is fairly uncommon, but Agastya uses it twice elsewhere (I.167.10, I.182.8); the rather more common ├бnu тИЪbh┼л can mean тАШbe devoted toтАЩ (тЖР тАШfollowтАЩ), and that seems to be the sense here.

Most interpr. take ├бtapyam─Бne as тАШfree from sufferingтАЩ, but the more literal meaning of тИЪtap тАШbe hot, scorchтАЩ seems appropriate in the solar context I see here.

In тАЬthe pair among the godsтАЭ (ubh├й dev─Б╠Бn─Бm), referring to Heaven and Earth, ubh├й тАШpairтАЩ is dual, while in тАЬalong with the pairs among the daysтАЭ (ubh├бyebhir ├бhn─Бm) тАШpairsтАЩ (ubh├бyebhiс╕е) is plural. This is presumably because Heaven and Earth are a unique pair, whereas the two day-halves, Day and Night, are recurrent and can be thought of as multiple pairs – though the dual can also be used of them, as in ├бhan─л in 1d.

Griffith

May we be close to both the Worlds who suffer no pain, Parents of Gods, who aid with favour,
Both mid the Gods, with Day and Night alternate. Protect us, Heaven and Earth, from fearful danger.

Macdonell

May we be near to both the worlds who suffer No care, parents of gods, who aid with favour. Both are divine, with days and nights alternate. O Heaven and Earth from dreadful darkness save us.

Geldner

Den beiden leidlosen, mit ihrem Schutze sch├╝tzenden Rodasi, den G├╢ttereltern, m├╢chten wir genehm sein, den beiden unter den G├╢ttern an beiden der Tagesh├дlften. - Himmel und Erde, bewahret uns vor ├Ьbergewalt!

Grassmann

Wir seien lieb den beiden sel’gen Welten, die huldvoll helfen, sie, der G├╢tter Aeltern, Den G├╢ttern eigen nebst der Nacht, dem Tage; beschirmt vor grauser Noth uns, Erd’ und Himmel!

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬGoing always together, equally young, and of the like termination, sisters, and kindred, and scenting the navel of the world, plural ced on their lap as its parents; defend us, Heaven and Earth, from great danger.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Scenting the navel: abhijighrant─л bhuvanasya n─Бbhim pitror upasthe: n─Бbhi = water, udakam, as the binding of all beings, bh┼лtaj─Бtasya bandhakam; this may be regarded as the child of heaven and earth, as they both contribute to its production: ubhayor udaka pradatvam prasiddham; or, the two here mentioned may imply water and the oblation, which are also connected

Jamison Brereton

The two young women, sisters, siblings [=Night and Dawn?],
contiguous and uniting with each other in the lap of their parents,
sniff-kissing the navel of the world. тАУ O Heaven and Earth, protect us from the formless void.

Griffith

Faring together, young, with meeting limits, Twin Sisters lying in their Parents’ bosom,
Kissing the centre of the world together. Protect us, Heaven and Earth, from fearful danger.

Macdonell

Maidens uniting, with adjoining limits, Twin sisters, resting in their parents’ bosom, They kiss, combined, the universe’s centre. O Heaven and Earth, from dreadful darkness save us.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI invoke to the sacrifice, for the preservation of gods (and men), the two vast, all-supporting, and mighty parents (of the rain and corn); who, beautiful in form, sustain ambrosial (showers); defend us, Heaven and Earth, from great danger.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The two broad and lofty seats do I invoke with truth, the begetters of the gods with their help,
they of lovely countenance who conceive the immortal one. тАУ O Heaven and Earth, protect us from the formless void.

Griffith

Duly I call the two wide seats, the mighty, the general Parents, with the God’s protection.
Who, beautiful to look on, make the nectar. Protect us, Heaven and Earth, from fearful danger.

Macdonell

Devoutly I the two seats wide and lofty, The parents of the gods, invoke with fervour, Who, fair of aspect, grant us life immortal. Heaven and Earth, from dreadful darkness save us.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI glorify with reverence, at this sacrifice, (the two), who are vast, expansive, multiform, infinite, auspicious;who support (all beings) by their bounty; defend us, Heaven and Earth, from great danger.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The two, broad and wide, voluminous and of distant boundary, do I address with homage in this sacrifice,
who, bringing good fortune and advancing well, conceive (the
embryo). тАУ O Heaven and Earth, protect us from the formless void.

Griffith

Wide, vast, and manifold, whose bounds are distant,–these, reverent, I address at this our worship,
The blessed Pair, victorious, all-sustaining. Protect us, Heaven and Earth, from fearful danger.

Macdonell

Them wide and broad and great, whose bounds are distant, Who, beautiful and fain to help, grant blessings: I at this sacrifice invoke with homage. O Heaven and Earth, from dreadful darkness save us.

Geldner

Den weiten, breiten, ger├дumigen, fernbegrenzten spreche ich unter Verbeugung bei diesem Opfer eine Bitte aus, die gl├╝ckbringend allen weit voran sind, den Keim empfangen. - Himmel und Erde, bewahret uns vor ├Ьbergewalt!

Grassmann

Die weiten, breiten, grossen, fernbegrenzten ruf’ ich mit Ehrfurcht an bei diesem Opfer; Die seligen, die h├╝lfreich gern gew├дhren, beschirmt vor grauser Noth uns, Erd’ und Himmel!

English translation:

тАЬMay this sacrifice be the means of expiating those offences which we may have committed against the gods, against a friend at any time, against a son-in-law; defend us, Heaven and Earth, from great danger.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

A son-in-law: jaspatim v─Б: j─Бс╕е = daughters;

Patim = lord or husband

Jamison Brereton

If we have ever committed any offence at all against the gods or against a comrade or against the lord of the family,
this hymnic vision should be propitiation to them. тАУ O Heaven and
Earth, protect us from the formless void.

Griffith

What sin we have at any time committed against the Gods, our friend, our house’s chieftain,
Thereof may this our hymn be expiation. Protect us, Heaven and Earth, from fearful danger.

Macdonell

If ever we have any sin committed Against the gods, or friend, or house’s chieftain. Of that may this our hymn be expiation. O Heaven and Earth, from dreadful darkness save us.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay both these, accepting praise, and friendly to man, be favourable to me; may they both be associated as guardians for my protection; deities, we your adorers, propitiating you with (sacrificial) food, desire ample (wealth), for the sake of makign liberal donations.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let both lauds belonging to men help me; let both (Heaven and Earth) accompany me with aid, with help.
There is much for him who gives even more than the stranger. Becoming exhilarated by the refreshment, might we be refreshed, o gods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take ┼лt─л╠Бas dual nom. (Witzel Got┼Н тАЬbeide HilfenтАЭ), but Geldner allows the possibility of an instr. and Renou takes it as instr., as do I. English translation:

тАЬEndowed with understanding, I repeat to Heaven and Earth this initial praise, to be heard around; may paternal (heaven) and maternal (earth) preserve us from reprehensible iniquity; and ever nigh defend us with their protection.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I of good wisdom have spoken this truth to Heaven and to Earth to hear first.
Let the two of them protect from disgrace and difficulty in close
quarters. Let the mother and father guard (us) with their help.

Griffith

Endowed with understanding, I have uttered this truth, for all to hear, to Earth and Heaven.
Be near us, keep us from reproach and trouble. Father and Mother, with your help preserve us.

Macdonell

This truth have I now uttered first with wisdom To Heaven and Earth that every one may hear it. Protect me from disgrace and peril; guard me As Father and as Mother with your succour.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay this (hymn), Heaven and Earth,be successful; (the hymn) which, Father and Mother, I repeat to you both on this occasion; be ever with your protection in the proximity of those who praise you; that we may obtain food, strength, and long life.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

In the proximity of those: dev─Бn─Бm avame: the first is interpreted stotс╣Ыn─Бm = of praisers

Jamison Brereton

Let this come true, Heaven and Earth, which I address to you two, o Father and Mother.
Become the nearest of the gods with your help. тАУ May we know
refreshment and a community having lively waters.

Griffith

Be this my prayer fulfilled, O Earth and Heaven, wherewith, Father and Mother, I address you.
Nearest of Gods be ye with your protection. May we find strengthening food in full abundance.

Macdonell

May this my prayer come true, O Earth and Heaven, With which I here address you, Father, Mother. Be nearest of the gods to us with favours: May we find food and home with flowing water.

Geldner

Dies soll wahr werden, Himmel und Erde, worum ich euch hier bitte, Vater und Mutter! Seid die n├дchsten der G├╢tter mit euren Hilfen! - Wir m├╢chten einen gastfreien Opferb├╝ndler kennen lernen, der rasch schenkt.

Dies werde wahr nun, Himmel du und Erde, was ich zu euch, o Vater, Mutter, rede, Seid unter G├╢ttern uns durch Huld die n├дchsten. Gebt Labung uns und wasserreiche Fluren.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА) рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢ рдФрд░ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди (рдорд╛рддрдГ, рдкрд┐рддрдГ) рдорд╛рддрд╛ рдкрд┐рддрд╛рдУ ! рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдорд╛рддрд╛-рдкрд┐рддрд╛ рдЬрдм рд╕рдиреНрддрд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рдРрд╕рд╛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдХрд░реЗрдВ рдХрд┐ рдЬреЛ рд╣рдорд╛рд░реЗ рдзрд░реНрдордпреБрдХреНрдд рдХрд░реНрдо рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рд╣реА рддреБрдордХреЛ рд╕реЗрд╡рдиреЗ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗрдВ рдФрд░ рдирд╣реАрдВ рддрдерд╛ рд╕рдиреНрддрд╛рди рдкрд┐рддрд╛-рдорд╛рддрд╛ рдЖрджрд┐ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдкрд╛рд▓рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдРрд╕реЗ рдХрд╣реЗрдВ рдХрд┐ рдЬреЛ рд╣рдорд╛рд░реЗ рд╕рддреНрдп рдЖрдЪрд░рдг рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рд╣реА рддреБрдордХреЛ рдЖрдЪрд░рдг рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗрдВ рдФрд░ рдЙрдирд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рдкрд░реАрдд рдирд╣реАрдВ рее резрез реердЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рдХреЗ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрдд рд╕реЗ рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдФрд░ рдЙрддреНрдкрд╛рджрдХ рдХреЗ рдХрд░реНрдореЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рд╣реИ, рдпрд╣ рдЬрд╛рдирдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реердпрд╣ рдПрдХрд╕реМ рдкрдЪрд╛рд╕реАрд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рддреАрд╕рд░рд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рдЗрд╡ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреЗ рдорд╛рддрдГ рдкрд┐рддреЛ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдорд╡рдореЗ рднреВрддрдВ рдпрджрд┐рд╣ рд╡рд╛рдореБрдкрдмреНрд░реБрд╡реЗ рддрджрд┐рджрдВ рд╕рддреНрдпрдорд╕реНрддреБ рдпреЗрди рд╡рдпрдВ рдпреБрд╡рдпреЛрд░рд╡реЛрднрд┐рд░рд┐рд╖рдВ рд╡реГрдЬрдирдВ рдЬреАрд░рджрд╛рдиреБрдВ рдЪ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдо рее резрез рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрдерд╛рддреНрд░ рд╕рддреНрдпрдорд╛рддреНрд░реЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ ред

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЗрджрдореН) рдЬрдЧрддреН (рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрджрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ (рд╕рддреНрдпрдореН) (рдЕрд╕реНрддреБ) (рдкрд┐рддрдГ) рдкрд╛рд▓рдХ (рдорд╛рддрдГ) рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрдкреНрд░рджреЗ (рдпрддреН) (рдЗрд╣) (рдЙрдкрдмреНрд░реБрд╡реЗ) (рд╡рд╛рдореН) рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдореН (рднреВрддрдореН) рдирд┐рд╖реНрдкрдиреНрдирдореН (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдореН) рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛рдореН (рдЕрд╡рдореЗ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрд╡реНрдпреЗ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░реЗ (рдЕрд╡реЛрднрд┐рдГ) рдкрд╛рд▓рдиреИрдГ (рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдо) (рдЗрд╖рдореН) (рд╡реГрдЬрдирдореН) (рдЬреАрд░рджрд╛рдиреБрдореН) рее резрез рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдорд╛рддрд╛-рдкрд┐рддрд╛ рдпрд╛рдВрдиреА рд╕рдВрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВрдирд╛ рдЕрд╕рд╛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдХрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛ рдХреА рдЖрдордЪреНрдпрд╛ рдзрд░реНрдордпреБрдХреНрдд рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдВрдЪрд╛рдЪ рддреБрдореНрд╣реА рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рд╛, рдЗрддрд░ рдирд╡реНрд╣реЗ рд╡ рд╕рдВрддрд╛рди рдкрд┐рддрд╛-рдорд╛рддрд╛ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреАрдВрдиреА рдЖрдкрд▓реНрдпрд╛ рдкрд╛рд▓рдирдХрд░реНрддреНрдпрд╛рд▓рд╛ рдЕрд╕реЗ рдореНрд╣рдгрд╛рд╡реЗ рдХреА рдЬреЗ рдЖрдордЪреЗ рд╕рддреНрдп рдЖрдЪрд░рдг рдЖрд╣реЗ, рддреНрдпрд╛рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгреЗ рддреБрдореНрд╣реА рд╡рд╛рдЧрд╛ рддреНрдпрд╛рдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рд╛ рд╡реЗрдЧрд│реЗ рдирд╛рд╣реА. рее резрез рее
